Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
Classification of Attributes: Negative, Active, and Essential
Commentary classifies attributes relative to the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentary distinguishes negative and active attributes from essential attributes, and why existence is considered the essential attribute.

Core Idea
Negative and active attributes are 'other' to the essence, while existence is identical to the essence according to Ash'ari.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a key point in the classification of divine attributes. He explains that when we say 'attributes of the essence,' not all attributes are included. Negative attributes and attributes of action are considered 'other' for different reasons, while the essential attribute of existence is uniquely linked to the essence itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall classification.
Notice the three categories: negative, active, and essential.
2
Understand negative attributes
Focus on the first part: why negative attributes are 'other'. They are not subsistent in the essence because they are privative (absence of qualities).
Example: 'not being a body' is a negative attribute.
3
Understand attributes of acts
Attributes like giving life and causing death are 'other' because they are separable — they are temporal relations of power, not permanent qualities.
These attributes are contingent and not always present.
4
Grasp the essential attribute of existence
Existence is the essential attribute. According to Ash'ari, it is identical to the essence, not a separate addition. The commentator notes it's a mental consideration.
This contrasts with the Mu'tazila view that existence is separate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخرج بإضافة صفات لـ (الذات) : الصفات السلبية: فإنها (غير) بمعنى أنها ليست قائمة به؛ لأنها أمور عدمية، وصفاتُ الأفعال كالإحياء والإماتة، فإنها (غير) أيضاً، بمعنى أنها منفكة؛ لأنها هي تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة . والصفةُ النفسية وهي الوجود ؛ لأنها عين الموجود على كلام الأشعري، وقد تقدَّم أن التحقيق تأويله على معنى أنه ليس زائداً على الذات بحيث يُرى، فلا ينافي أنه أمر اعتباري، وغير الموجود على كلام غير الأشعري.
And by adding 'attributes' to 'the essence', what is excluded are: the negative attributes: for they are (other) in the sense that they are not subsistent through Him; because they are privative matters. And the attributes of acts such as giving life and causing death: for they are (other) as well, in the sense that they are separable; because they are the relations of the temporal determinative power. And the essential attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya), which is existence: for it is identical to the existent according to the statement of al-Ash'arī, and it has preceded that the verification is its interpretation to mean that it is not additional to the essence such that it is seen, so it does not contradict that it is a mental consideration, and it is other than the existent according to the statement of other than al-Ash'arī.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a classification of attributes with respect to the phrase 'attributes of the essence'. The commentary explains what is excluded by the addition of 'of the essence': (1) Negative attributes (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya) — they are considered 'other' because they are not qualities that subsist in the essence; they are privative, like 'not being a body'. (2) Attributes of acts (ṣifāt al-af‘āl), such as giving life and causing death — they are 'other' in the sense of being separable, because they are temporal relations of power (ta‘alluqāt al-qudra al-tanjīziyya al-ḥāditha). (3) The essential attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya), which is existence (al-wujūd) — according to al-Ash‘arī, existence is identical to the existent (the essence itself), not an additional attribute. The verification is that it is not a real addition such that it could be perceived separately; it is a mental consideration. But according to others (like the Mu‘tazila), it is other than the existent. This passage thus clarifies that the attributes of essence proper are only those that are inseparable and real, while negative and active attributes are not included in that category.

Key Terms
الصفات السلبية
صفات الأفعال
الصفة النفسية
الوجود
تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All attributes besides the essence are 'other' in the same sense.
Correction: Negative attributes are 'other' because they are not real attributes; active attributes are 'other' because they are temporally separable; existence is identical to the essence according to Ash'ari.

Checkpoint
Why are negative attributes considered 'other' (ghayr) according to this passage?
A) Because they are separable from the essence
B) Because they are not subsistent through the essence, being privative matters
C) Because they are identical to the essence
D) Because they are temporal relations

Key Takeaway
Negative and active attributes are excluded from 'attributes of the essence' for different reasons; only existence is truly the essence's own attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider God's attributes like giving life and causing death, do you realize they are temporary acts of His power, not eternal attributes? How does that change your awe of His moment-to-moment sovereignty?
?
Knowing that according to al-Ash'ari, existence is identical to God's essence, how does that challenge you to stop imagining God as having parts or qualities separate from His very being? What does that demand from your worship?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
Classification of Attributes: Negative, Active, Essential
Commentator classifies attributes into negative, active, and essential, explaining 'not other'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of divine attributes (negative, active, essential) and the meaning of the phrase that the attributes are 'not other' than the essence.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are not separate from Allah's essence, but not all are identical; they are 'not separable'.

In this passage from Tuhfat al-Mureed, the commentator breaks down the attributes of Allah into three kinds. He explains which are 'other' in the sense of being separable or privative, and which are 'not other' meaning inseparable from the essence. This sets the foundation for the Ash'ari understanding of the relationship between Allah and His attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the three categories listed at the beginning.
Focus on the words 'sifāt salbiyya', 'sifāt af'āl', and 'al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya'.
2
Identify each category's relationship to the essence
For each category, note whether the commentator says it is 'other' (ghayr) and in what sense. Negative attributes are 'other' because they are privative and not subsistent; action attributes are 'other' because they are separable; the essential attribute (existence) is 'not other' according to Ash'ari.
3
Understand the phrase 'not other'
The commentator explains that 'laysat bi-ghayr' means not separable (munfakk), not that the attributes are identical to the essence. This resolves a potential misunderstanding that the attributes are either identical or distinct in a way that implies separation.
This is the key doctrinal point of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخرج بإضافة صفات لـ (الذات) :
الصفات السلبية: فإنها (غير) بمعنى أنها ليست قائمة به؛ لأنها أمور عدمية، وصفاتُ الأفعال كالإحياء والإماتة، فإنها (غير) أيضاً، بمعنى أنها منفكة؛ لأنها هي تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة .
والصفةُ النفسية وهي الوجود ؛ لأنها عين الموجود على كلام الأشعري، وقد : تقدَّم أن التحقيق تأويله على معنى أنه ليس زائداً على الذات بحيث يُرى، فلا ينافي أنه أمر اعتباري، وغير الموجود على كلام غير الأشعري.
قوله : (لَيْسَتْ بِغَيْرِ) بلا تنوين لفظ (غير)، لإضافته تقديراً إلى مثل ما أضيف إليه (عين)، والتقدير : ليست بغير الذات، وقد عرفت أن المراد ليست بغير منفك، فلا ينافي أنها غير ملازم.
And what is excluded by adding attributes to the essence: the negative attributes: for they are 'other' in the sense that they are not subsistent in Him; because they are non-existent matters, and the attributes of actions like giving life and causing death, for they are also 'other' in the sense that they are separable; because they are the attachments of the determinant power that is contingent. And the essential attribute is existence; for it is identical to the existent according to the statement of al-Ash'ari, and it has preceded that the verified position is to interpret it as meaning that it is not additional to the essence in a way that it is seen, so it does not contradict that it is a relational matter, and it is other than the existent according to the statement of other than al-Ash'ari. His statement: (not other) without nunation of the word (other), due to its being in genitive construction in estimation to what (identical) is added to, and the estimation: they are not other than the essence, and you have known that the intended meaning is they are not other in the sense of being separable, so it does not contradict that they are non-separable.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a classification and definition of the types of divine attributes, explaining the meaning of the phrase 'not other' (laysat bi-ghayr). The commentator first states what is excluded by adding attributes to the essence. He lists three categories: negative attributes (like existence not being a body, etc.), which are 'other' in that they are privative and not subsistent in the essence; attributes of action (like giving life and causing death), which are 'other' in that they are separable from the essence as they are contingent attachments; and the essential attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya), which is existence itself. According to al-Ash'ari, existence is identical to the existent (i.e., not additional), but the verified interpretation is that it is not additional in a way that it is seen as separate, so it is a relational concept. Then he explains the phrase 'not other' from the matn: it means the attributes of meaning are not other than the essence in the sense of being separable or independent entities. They are non-separable (ghayr munfakk), though they are not identical either. This sets the stage for the Mu'tazilite objection.

Key Terms
صفات سلبية
صفات الأفعال
الصفة النفسية
غير
منفك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'attributes are not other than the essence' means the attributes are identical to the essence.
Correction: It means they are not separable from the essence, not that they are identical. The attributes are distinct but inseparable.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does the phrase 'the attributes are not other (laysat bi-ghayr) than the essence' mean?
A) They are identical to the essence.
B) They are completely separate from the essence.
C) They are not separable from the essence, though not identical.
D) They are contingent beings.

Key Takeaway
The essential attribute is not separable from the essence, while negative and action attributes are 'other' in different senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's attributes like 'Al-Khāliq' (The Creator), do you imagine this attribute as something added to His essence that comes and goes with acts of creation? How does this lesson's distinction between inseparable and separable attributes challenge that image? What will you actively remind yourself of when reciting His names?
?
The passage clarifies that negative attributes are 'non-existent matters'—they only tell us what Allah is not. Is your heart content with knowing Allah through negations, or do you find yourself trying to imagine Him positively? What does this reveal about your own need for a concrete image, and how will you train yourself to embrace the transcendence?
?
You have learned that the essential attribute (existence) is not other than the essence, but also not identical in a way that denies relational aspects. In your act of worship, do you sometimes treat Allah's attributes as if they are separate 'parts'? Pledge one specific change in how you speak or think about Allah's oneness (tawḥīd) to align with the Ash'ari balance.

Divine Attributes

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Doubt on Eternal Attributes
Commentator presents and refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that eternal attributes imply multiple eternal beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari theologians refute the Mu'tazilite objection that affirming eternal attributes leads to polytheism.

Core Idea
Affirming eternal attributes does not imply multiple gods because attributes are not independent entities.

The Mu'tazilites argued that if God's attributes are eternal, then we have multiple eternal beings, akin to the Christian Trinity. This lesson presents the objection and the Ash'ari response, showing that the key is understanding that attributes are not 'other' as separate entities.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite Objection
Understand the dilemma: if attributes are contingent, that's impossible; if eternal, then multiple eternal beings.
Notice the dichotomy they present.
2
Note the Christian Comparison
The Mu'tazilites compare to the Trinity and argue that more than three eternal beings is worse.
This is an expansion of the argument.
3
Study the Ash'ari Response
Al-Sa'd explains that only independent eternal beings break tawhid; attributes are not independent, so no multiplicity.
Focus on the concept of 'otherness' (ghayriyya).
4
Understand the Clarification on Ghayriyya vs. Ayniyya
The negation of otherness is the core answer; negation of identity is extra, not part of the refutation.
This nuance is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف بذلك إلى الجواب عن الشبهة التي أوردها المعتزلة النافون لصفات المعاني، وتقريرها أن تقول : الصفاتُ الوجودية إما أن تكون حادثة فيلزم قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى، وإما أن تكون قديمة فيلزم تعدد القدماء، وهو كفر بإجماع المسلمين، وقد كفرت النصارى بزيادة قديمين على الذات العليَّةِ، فكفروا بإثبات آلهة ثلاثة كما قال تعالى: ﴿لَقَدْ كفَرَ الَّذِينَ قَالُوا إِنَّ اللهَ ثَالِثُ ثَلَثَةُ [المائدة: ۷۳] ، وإذا كفرت النصارى بإثبات آلهة ثلاثة، فكيف بالأكثر؛ وهو ثمانية قدماء الذات والصفات السبع، أو تسع بزيادة التكوين، أو عشر بزيادة الإدراك؟ فيلزم على إثبات ذلك (۱) الكفر من باب أولى، وهذا توسع في الدائرة؛ لأن أهل السنة معترفون بقِدَم الصفات . وحاصل الجواب كما أشار إليه العلامة السعد : أن المحظور المبطل للتوحيد إنما هو تعدد القدماء المتغايرة المنفكة بحيث تكون ذوات مستقلة، وليست الصفات مغايرة للذات بهذا المعنى، فلم يلزم التعدد المبطل للتوحيد حتى يلزم الكفر، فنفي الغيرية هو الذي أشير به للجواب عن الشبهة المذكورة، ولا مدخل لنفي العينية في الجواب، لكنه تكميل للفائدة
And the author pointed by that to the answer to the doubt that the Mu'tazilites who deny the attributes of meaning raised, and its formulation is that one says: The existential attributes are either contingent, which would entail the occurrence of contingent things in His essence (exalted), or they are eternal, which would entail the multiplicity of eternal beings, and that is disbelief by consensus of the Muslims. The Christians were disbelieved for adding two eternal beings to the supreme essence, thus they disbelieved for affirming three gods as He said: 'They have disbelieved who say Allah is the third of three' (5:73). And if the Christians were disbelieved for affirming three gods, then what about more—eight eternal beings: the essence and the seven attributes, or nine with the addition of takwīn, or ten with the addition of idrāk? Thus affirming that would entail disbelief all the more. This is an expansion of the circle because the Ahl al-Sunna acknowledge the eternity of the attributes. The summary of the answer as indicated by al-ʿAllāma al-Saʿd is that the prohibited thing that nullifies tawḥīd is only the multiplicity of eternal beings that are distinct and separable such that they are independent essences. The attributes are not other than the essence in that sense, so the multiplicity that nullifies tawḥīd does not occur such that disbelief follows. Thus the negation of otherness (ghayriyya) is what is pointed to as the answer to the mentioned doubt, and the negation of identity (ʿayniyya) has no entry in the answer, but it is a completion of benefit.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from the Mu'tazilites and the Ash'ari response. The objection: If attributes of meaning are affirmed as eternal, then either they are contingent (which is impossible for God) or eternal. If eternal, then we have multiple eternal beings (the essence and the attributes), which is akin to the Christian trinity and thus disbelief. The Mu'tazilites argue that since Christians were disbelieved for three, then eight or more is worse. The answer from al-Saʿd: The prohibition is against multiple eternal beings that are separate, independent entities. The attributes of God are not independent; they are not 'other' (ghayr) in the sense of being separate. They are not distinct essences. Therefore, affirming them does not entail the condemned multiplicity. The commentator clarifies that the negation of otherness (i.e., attributes are not other than the essence) is the key to the refutation, not the negation of identity. The negation of identity (i.e., they are not the essence either) is added as a completion, not as part of the answer.

Key Terms
تعدد القدماء
شبهة
غيرية
عينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming eternal attributes necessarily implies multiple gods.
Correction: Only if the attributes are independent entities; Ash'ari attributes are not independent.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does affirming eternal attributes not lead to the multiplicity of eternal beings (taʿaddud al-qudamā')?
A) Because the attributes are contingent.
B) Because the attributes are identical to the essence.
C) Because the attributes are not separate independent entities.
D) Because the attributes are only negative.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite objection fails because eternal attributes are not separate independent beings, so they do not create a multiplicity of gods.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat Allah's attributes like separate 'things' in your mind, as if His knowledge is a book He consults or His power is a tool He uses? How can you train yourself to see each attribute as a description of His very essence, not an add-on? What specific dhikr or contemplation will you practice this week to unify your awareness of Allah's attributes with His oneness?
?
The Mu'tazilites were so afraid of falling into shirk that they denied the attributes altogether. Are there Islamic teachings you feel tempted to reject or reinterpret because they seem too close to something forbidden? Where might your caution actually lead you to overcorrect and miss the truth? What will you do to test your own assumptions against the precise wording of scholars like al-Sa'd?
?
The core answer here hinges on the nuance of 'otherness' (ghayriyya). Are you patient enough to wrestle with theological subtleties rather than jumping to a comfortable but inaccurate conclusion? When you encounter a difficult doctrinal point, do you dismiss it or truly wrestle with it? What concrete step will you take this week to deepen your understanding of a nuanced aqeedah topic you've avoided?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
Attributes Are Not Identical to the Essence
Commentator explains that attributes are not identical to the essence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the phrase 'or identical to the essence' in the matn means the attributes are not identical to the essence, and the grammatical rule that 'or' can mean 'and' after negation.

Core Idea
Attributes are not identical to the essence; the word 'or' here means 'and'.

The commentator begins by clarifying a key phrase from the matn: 'or identical to the essence.' This might seem ambiguous, but he explains that it actually negates identity. Understanding this grammatical point is essential for grasping the early Maturidi position on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic sentence carefully. Notice the phrase 'أَوْ بِعَيْنِ الذَّاتِ' and the commentator's explanation that 'أَوْ' here means 'الواو' (and) because it comes after negation.
This is a common grammatical rule in Arabic.
2
Understand the negation
The commentator asserts that the attributes are not the same as the essence. Reflect on why this distinction matters in Islamic theology.
This sets the stage for later discussions on the modality of attributes.
3
Test your understanding
Try to rephrase the sentence in your own words without losing the meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: (أَوْ بِعَيْنِ الذَّاتِ) أي: وليست الصفات عين الذات، فـ (أو) بمعنى الواو؛ لأنَّ القاعدة أنها تكون بمعنى الواو بعد النفي.
واعلم أن وجوب صفات المعاني ذاتي لها ؛ مثل وجوب (۱) الذات، كما هو الحق الذي عليه السنوسي ومن تبعه وليست ممكنة لذاتها واجبة لغيرها بسبب اقتضاء الذات لها كما قاله العضد وهذه نزعةٌ من نزغات العضد، وسَرَتْ له هذه النزعة من كلام الفلاسفة، فإنهم يقولون : إن العالم ممكن لذاته، قديم لغيره ؛ بسبب كونه معلولاً لعلة قديمة؛ وهي ذاته تعالى، وما كان معلولاً لعلة قديمة فهو قديم، وهذا كلام باطل، وكلام السعد في موضع يوافق كلام العضد، وفي موضع آخر يوافق كلام السنوسي، وهو الذي تلقى الله عليه .
And His statement: (or identical to the essence) meaning: the attributes are not identical to the essence, so (or) is in the sense of (and); because the rule is that it comes in the sense of (and) after negation. And know that the necessity of the attributes of meaning is intrinsic to them, like the necessity of the essence, as is the truth upon which al-Sanūsī and those who followed him are, and they are not contingent in themselves and necessary through another due to the essence's requiring them as al-ʿAḍud said. This is a streak of the streaks of al-ʿAḍud, and this streak came to him from the speech of the philosophers, for they say: The world is contingent in itself, eternal through another, because it is an effect of an eternal cause, namely His essence (exalted), and what is an effect of an eternal cause is eternal. This is false speech. And al-Saʿd's speech in one place agrees with al-ʿAḍud, and in another place agrees with al-Sanūsī, and that is what he was taught by Allah.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage covers two points. First, the commentator explains the matn's phrase 'or identical to the essence' — it means the attributes are not identical to the essence; the word 'or' here functions like 'and' because after negation it can mean conjunction. Second, he addresses a theological dispute about the modality (wujūb) of the attributes. The correct view (of al-Sanūsī) is that the attributes of meaning are necessary (wājib) in themselves, just as the essence is necessary in itself. They are not contingent (mumkin) in themselves and necessary through another by virtue of the essence's requiring them, as claimed by al-ʿAḍud. The commentator criticizes al-ʿAḍud's view as influenced by philosophers who say the world is contingent in itself but eternal through its eternal cause. The commentator deems this false. He notes that al-Saʿd (al-Taftazānī) had contradictory positions on this, but the one in agreement with al-Sanūsī is the correct one.

Key Terms
أَوْ بِعَيْنِ الذَّاتِ
الواو
النفي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'or identical' might suggest that attributes could alternatively be identical to the essence.
Correction: The commentator explains that 'or' here is not a disjunction but a conjunction after negation, so it emphasizes that attributes are not identical.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the function of the word 'أَو' in the phrase 'أَوْ بِعَيْنِ الذَّاتِ'?
A) It indicates a choice between two possibilities.
B) It means 'and' because it comes after negation.
C) It means 'or' in the normal disjunctive sense.
D) It means 'except'.

Key Takeaway
The matn's phrase 'or identical to the essence' actually denies identity; 'or' functions as 'and' after negation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals a subtle linguistic rule that changes the meaning of a statement about Allah. How does this challenge you to approach theological texts with greater care? What practical steps will you take to ensure you do not misinterpret Allah's attributes due to casual reading?
?
The phrase 'or identical to the essence' could easily be misunderstood as offering an option. Reflect on a time when you misunderstood a religious text because you assumed a common meaning for a word. How does this lesson encourage you to seek deeper understanding before forming beliefs about Allah?

The Nature of the Necessity of Attributes
Commentator discusses the modality of attributes and criticizes al-ʿAḍud's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disputed nature of the necessity (wujūb) of the attributes of meaning: whether they are necessary in themselves (like the essence) or necessary through another (by the essence's requirement).

Core Idea
The attributes of meaning are necessary in themselves, not contingent made necessary by the essence.

After establishing that attributes are not identical to the essence, the commentator addresses a deeper theological issue: Are the attributes necessary (wājib) in themselves, or are they contingent (mumkin) made necessary by the essence? This point was disputed by al-ʿAḍud and al-Sanūsī, with the commentator siding with the latter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage from 'واعلم' to the end. Notice the two opposing views and the commentator's criticism of al-ʿAḍud's position.
This passage is more polemical than the previous one.
2
Identify the two positions
Al-Sanūsī holds that attributes are necessary in themselves (wājib bi-dhātihā) like the essence. Al-ʿAḍud holds they are contingent in themselves but necessary through another (wājib bi-ghayrihā) because the essence requires them.
The commentator considers al-ʿAḍud's view influenced by philosophers.
3
Understand the critique
The commentator connects al-ʿAḍud's view to the philosophical claim that the world is contingent in itself but eternal through its cause. He calls this false.
This shows the stakes: attributing contingency to attributes risks similarities to philosophical cosmology.
4
Reflect on al-Taftazānī's position
The commentator notes that al-Taftazānī (al-Saʿd) had conflicting statements, but the correct one agrees with al-Sanūsī.
This highlights the authority of al-Sanūsī in the later tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: (أَوْ بِعَيْنِ الذَّاتِ) أي: وليست الصفات عين الذات، فـ (أو) بمعنى الواو؛ لأنَّ القاعدة أنها تكون بمعنى الواو بعد النفي.
واعلم أن وجوب صفات المعاني ذاتي لها ؛ مثل وجوب (۱) الذات، كما هو الحق الذي عليه السنوسي ومن تبعه وليست ممكنة لذاتها واجبة لغيرها بسبب اقتضاء الذات لها كما قاله العضد وهذه نزعةٌ من نزغات العضد، وسَرَتْ له هذه النزعة من كلام الفلاسفة، فإنهم يقولون : إن العالم ممكن لذاته، قديم لغيره ؛ بسبب كونه معلولاً لعلة قديمة؛ وهي ذاته تعالى، وما كان معلولاً لعلة قديمة فهو قديم، وهذا كلام باطل، وكلام السعد في موضع يوافق كلام العضد، وفي موضع آخر يوافق كلام السنوسي، وهو الذي تلقى الله عليه .
And His statement: (or identical to the essence) meaning: the attributes are not identical to the essence, so (or) is in the sense of (and); because the rule is that it comes in the sense of (and) after negation. And know that the necessity of the attributes of meaning is intrinsic to them, like the necessity of the essence, as is the truth upon which al-Sanūsī and those who followed him are, and they are not contingent in themselves and necessary through another due to the essence's requiring them as al-ʿAḍud said. This is a streak of the streaks of al-ʿAḍud, and this streak came to him from the speech of the philosophers, for they say: The world is contingent in itself, eternal through another, because it is an effect of an eternal cause, namely His essence (exalted), and what is an effect of an eternal cause is eternal. This is false speech. And al-Saʿd's speech in one place agrees with al-ʿAḍud, and in another place agrees with al-Sanūsī, and that is what he was taught by Allah.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage covers two points. First, the commentator explains the matn's phrase 'or identical to the essence' — it means the attributes are not identical to the essence; the word 'or' here functions like 'and' because after negation it can mean conjunction. Second, he addresses a theological dispute about the modality (wujūb) of the attributes. The correct view (of al-Sanūsī) is that the attributes of meaning are necessary (wājib) in themselves, just as the essence is necessary in itself. They are not contingent (mumkin) in themselves and necessary through another by virtue of the essence's requiring them, as claimed by al-ʿAḍud. The commentator criticizes al-ʿAḍud's view as influenced by philosophers who say the world is contingent in itself but eternal through its eternal cause. The commentator deems this false. He notes that al-Saʿd (al-Taftazānī) had contradictory positions on this, but the one in agreement with al-Sanūsī is the correct one.

Key Terms
وجوب
ذاتي
ممكن
واجب بغيره
العضد
السنوسي
السعد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attributes are contingent (mumkin) in themselves and become necessary because the essence requires them.
Correction: The correct view is that attributes are necessary in themselves (wājib bi-dhātihā), just like the essence. They are not dependent on the essence for their necessity.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the source of al-ʿAḍud's view that attributes are contingent in themselves and necessary through another?
A) The Muʿtazila
B) The philosophers (falāsifa)
C) The Ashʿarites
D) The Māturīdites

Key Takeaway
Attributes of meaning are necessary in themselves, not contingent made necessary by the essence; this preserves their perfection and avoids philosophical errors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever unconsciously treat God's attributes as secondary additions to His essence, as if He could have been without them? How does realizing their intrinsic necessity reshape your understanding of His perfection and your worship?
?
If you truly believed that each attribute of God is as necessary as His very existence, would your trust in Him be any different? What attribute do you most struggle to see as essential and unchangeable?
?
When you read that some scholars adopted a philosophical view that makes attributes dependent, does it challenge your own intellectual humility? Are you willing to submit your reason to the revealed truths even when they seem paradoxical?

The Attachment of Divine Power to Possibles
Commentator introduces attachments and states verifiers' position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what is meant by the attachment (taʿalluq) of divine attributes and why the verifiers restrict it to attributes of meaning (maʿānī) only.

Core Idea
Only attributes of meaning (maʿānī) have attachment; maʿnawiyya attributes do not.

The commentator begins a new section on how divine attributes relate to their objects. The matn verse states that power attaches to possibles without end. The commentary then addresses a subtle but crucial theological point: which kind of attribute actually has attachment? The verifiers clarify that it is only the attributes of meaning, not the derivative attributes (maʿnawiyya).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice that the matn verse is concise, and the commentary expands on it.
2
Identify the main claim
Identify the verdict of the verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn): attachment is for the maʿānī only. Contrast this with the other opinion (maʿnawiyya) and the unanimous denial of both.
3
Understand the reasoning
Understand why two attachments (to both maʿnā and maʿnawiyya) would be impossible: it would imply two agents acting on one effect, which is absurd in divine attributes.
The text cuts off, but the logic is clear.
4
Reflect on the implication
Reflect on why this distinction matters for understanding divine power. It upholds tawḥīd by avoiding multiplicity in the divine essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تعلقات الصفات
تعلقات القدرة]
+
۳۳ - فَقُدْرةٌ بِمُمْكِن تَعَلَّقَتْ بِلا تَنَاهِي مَا بِهِ تَعَلَّقَتْ
قوله : (فَقُدْرةٌ ... إلخ) أي : إذا أردت معرفة تعلقات الصفات، فأقول لك: (قدرة ... إلى آخره)، فالفاء فاء الفصيحة، ولما طوى ذيل مباحث الصفات، شرع في نشر ما لها من التعلقات .
والذي اعتمده المحققون أن التعلق للمعاني فقط، وقال بعض المتكلمين: للمعنوية، ولم يقل أحدٌ بأن التعلق للمعاني والمعنوية معاً، وإلا لزم اجتماع مؤثرين على أثر واحدٍ في القدرة والكون قادراً، والإرادة والكون مريداً، ولزم تحصيل
Explanation of the attachments of the attributes. Attachments of power.] + 33 - So power is attached to a possible without end to what it is attached to. His statement: (So power ... etc.) meaning: If you want to know the attachments of the attributes, I say to you: (power ... to the end), so the fa is the fa of eloquent speech, and since he folded the tail of the discussions of the attributes, he began to spread what pertains to them of attachments. And what the verifiers relied upon is that the attachment is for the [attributes of] meaning only, and some theologians said: for the attribute-of-meaning-with-addition (maʿnawiyya). No one said that the attachment is for both meaning and maʿnawiyya together, otherwise it would entail the combination of two agents on one effect in power and being powerful, and will and being willing, and it would entail obtaining...
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section on the attachments (taʿalluqāt) of the divine attributes. The commentator quotes the matn verse: 'So power is attached to a possible without end to what it is attached to.' He explains that the fa (so) is the fa of eloquent speech, introducing the topic after concluding the discussion on the attributes themselves. Then he presents a key theological point: the verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn) hold that the attachment (taʿalluq) pertains only to the attributes of meaning (al-maʿānī) themselves, not to the attribute-of-meaning-with-addition (al-maʿnawiyya). Some theologians said it pertains to the maʿnawiyya, but no one said it pertains to both simultaneously, because that would imply two agents acting on one effect, which is impossible. The text cuts off, but the argument continues that if both power and being powerful (qudra and kawn qādiran) were attached to the same possible, there would be two agents, which is absurd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the attribute of meaning (e.g., power) and the attribute-of-meaning-with-addition (e.g., being powerful) both have attachment to the same object.
Correction: The verifiers state that attachment belongs only to the attribute of meaning, not to both, because that would entail two agents on one effect, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the verifiers, what is the correct view on the attachment (taʿalluq) of divine attributes?
A) It belongs to both the attribute of meaning (maʿnā) and the attribute-of-meaning-with-addition (maʿnawiyya).
B) It belongs only to the attribute-of-meaning-with-addition (maʿnawiyya).
C) It belongs only to the attribute of meaning (maʿnā).
D) It belongs to neither.

Key Takeaway
The attachment of divine attributes pertains only to intrinsic attributes of meaning (maʿānī), not to derived attributes (maʿnawiyya), safeguarding divine simplicity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is powerful,' do you realize that this description (maʿnawiyya) is merely a reflection of His intrinsic power (maʿnā) and not a second thing? How does this deepen your awareness of His oneness?
?
The verifiers insisted that attachment belongs only to attributes of meaning, not to derived descriptions. Are there areas in your faith where you unconsciously treat Allah's descriptions as separate 'parts' of Him? What will you do to realign your understanding?
?
If the attachment of power were to both the attribute and the description, it would imply two agents for one effect—a denial of tawḥīd. Examine your heart: have you ever acted as if something other than Allah has independent power over your life? How does this lesson correct you?

Attributes: Neither Other Nor Identical to Essence
Explains the two negations and the linguistic rule of 'أو'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise meaning of the formula that attributes are neither other than nor identical to the essence and how this preserves tawhid.

Core Idea
Attributes are not separate entities, nor are they the essence itself.

In this passage, the commentator explains the key formula used to describe the relationship between Allah's attributes and His essence. He shows that the negation of otherness directly answers a common doubt, while the negation of identity is a supplementary clarification. We will unpack the logical distinction and the linguistic rule behind the phrase 'أو بعين الذات'.

Guided Path
1
Read and translate the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Then read the translation to understand the literal meaning.
2
Identify the two negations
The passage mentions two negations: attributes are not other than the essence and not identical to the essence. Notice that the negation of otherness is the primary answer to the doubt about multiplicity.
3
Analyze the linguistic point
The commentator explains that 'أو' in the phrase 'أو بعين الذات' means 'and' because it comes after negation. Understand the rule that 'أو' takes the meaning of 'واو' after negation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذوات مستقلة، وليست الصفات مغايرة للذات بهذا المعنى، فلم يلزم التعدد المبطل للتوحيد حتى يلزم الكفر، فنفي الغيرية هو الذي أشير به للجواب عن الشبهة المذكورة، ولا مدخل لنفي العينية في الجواب، لكنه تكميل للفائدة، على أن الغرض الأصلي كما علمت بيان حكم الصفات وهو أنها ليست بغير الذات ولا بعين الذات، ولم يذكر المصنف مغايرة بعض الصفات لبعض لظهور ذلك.
وقوله: (أَوْ بِعَيْنِ الذَّاتِ) أي: وليست الصفات عين الذات، فـ (أو) بمعنى الواو؛ لأنَّ القاعدة أنها تكون بمعنى الواو بعد النفي.
واعلم أن وجوب صفات المعاني ذاتي لها ؛ مثل وجوب (1) الذات، كما كما هو الحق الذي عليه السنوسي ومن تبعه وليست ممكنة لذاتها واجبة لغيرها بسبب اقتضاء الذات لها كما قاله العضد وهذه نزعةٌ من نزغات العضد، وسَرَتْ له هذه النزعة من كلام الفلاسفة، فإنهم يقولون : إن العالم ممكن لذاته، قديم لغيره ؛ بسبب كونه معلولاً لعلة قديمة؛ وهي ذاته تعالى، وما كان معلولاً لعلة قديمة فهو قديم، وهذا كلام باطل، وكلام السعد في موضع يوافق كلام العضد، وفي موضع آخر يوافق كلام السنوسي، وهو الذي تلقى الله عليه .
Independent entities, and the attributes are not different from the essence in this sense, so the multiplicity that invalidates tawhid did not follow, such that unbelief would follow. So the negation of otherness is what is referred to in the answer to the mentioned doubt, and the negation of identity has no entry in the answer, but it is a completion of the benefit, while the original purpose, as you know, is to explain the ruling of the attributes, which is that they are not other than the essence nor identical to the essence, and the author did not mention the difference of some attributes from others due to its obviousness.
And his saying: (or identical to the essence) means: the attributes are not the essence itself, so (أو) is in the meaning of (الواو), because the rule is that it is in the meaning of (الواو) after negation.
And know that the necessity of the attributes of meanings is intrinsic to them, like the necessity (1) of the essence, as is the truth upon which al-Sanusi and those who follow him are, and they are not possible in themselves and necessary for other than themselves due to the essence's requirement for them as al-'Adud said. And this is a deviation from among the deviations of al-'Adud, and this deviation came to him from the speech of the philosophers, for they say: the world is possible in itself, eternal due to other than itself, due to its being an effect of an eternal cause, which is His essence, exalted, and whatever is an effect of an eternal cause is eternal. And this is false speech. And the speech of al-Sa'd in one place agrees with the speech of al-'Adud, and in another place agrees with the speech of al-Sunusi, and that is what he received from Allah upon him.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage addresses two key points about the divine attributes: first, that they are neither identical to the essence nor other than it in a way that implies multiplicity of gods; second, that the attributes of meanings (صفات المعاني) are necessary in themselves like the essence, not contingent. The author begins by affirming that attributes are not independent entities distinct from the essence in the sense that would imply plurality contradicting tawhid. The negation of otherness (غيرية) is the direct answer to the doubt that attributes imply multiple gods. The negation of identity (عينية) is an additional clarification, not the primary response. Then he explains the phrase "أو بعين الذات" from the poem, noting that "أو" here means "and" because it comes after negation. He then moves to a critical issue: the necessity of the attributes. He follows al-Sanusi in affirming that the necessity of the attributes is intrinsic (ذاتي) like the necessity of the essence. He rejects al-'Adud's view that attributes are contingent in themselves but necessary due to the essence's requirement. This view, he says, is a deviation inspired by the philosophers who claim the world is possible in itself but eternal due to its cause. This is false. He notes that al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) sometimes agrees with al-'Adud and sometimes with al-Sanusi, and the latter is the accepted position.

Key Terms
الغيرية
العينية
صفات المعاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The attributes are either separate beings or exactly the essence.
Correction: They are not independent entities but also not identical; they are a distinct category.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the negation of identity (عينية) not the primary answer to the doubt about multiplicity?
A) Because it is not correct
B) Because the negation of otherness already suffices
C) Because it leads to another doubt
D) Because the attributes are identical to the essence

Key Takeaway
The attributes are neither separate entities nor the essence itself; the negation of otherness safeguards tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's attributes like His knowledge or power, do you ever unconsciously picture them as separate 'things' existing alongside Him? If so, how does this lesson's negation of otherness challenge that mental image and call you to purify your tawhid?
?
The negation of identity means God's attributes are not exactly His essence—they do not exhaust who He is. Are you content with the mystery that God is greater than what you can comprehend? Or do you secretly wish to reduce Him to something fully graspable?
?
If the negation of otherness is the primary answer to doubts about multiplicity, and the negation of identity is a 'completion of benefit,' then what does it reveal about your own spiritual condition if you focus more on the secondary point and neglect the primary? Where in your life do you prioritize peripheral religious discussions over the core of tawhid?

The Intrinsic Necessity of the Attributes
Discusses the intrinsic necessity of attributes and refutes al-'Adud's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attributes of meanings are necessary in themselves and why al-'Adud's view that they are contingent is erroneous.

Core Idea
The attributes are just as necessary as the essence itself.

After clarifying the relationship of attributes to the essence, the commentator addresses a deeper issue: the mode of existence of the attributes. Al-Sanusi holds that the necessity of the attributes is intrinsic, while al-'Adud claims they are contingent but necessitated by the essence. The commentator refutes al-'Adud's view, linking it to the philosophers' view on the world's possibility and eternality. This lesson explores that controversy.

Guided Path
1
Read and translate the passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the literal meaning.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage contrasts two positions: al-Sanusi's view that attributes are intrinsically necessary, and al-'Adud's view that they are possible in themselves but necessary due to the essence. Note how the commentator aligns with al-Sanusi.
3
Understand the refutation
The commentator says al-'Adud's view is a deviation from the philosophers who claim the world is possible but eternal due to its cause. Recognize why this is considered false.
Also note al-Sa'd's inconsistency.

Definition of Ta'alluq: Only Meaning-Attributes Have Relation
Defines ta'alluq and argues it is only for meaning-attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verifiers defined ta'alluq (relation) and why they restricted it to meaning-attributes (المعاني) alone.

Core Idea
An attribute's relation is its request for an extra matter, and only meaning-attributes have such a request.

Before listing the types of relations, the author establishes what 'relation' means in kalam. This is not a trivial definition—it settles a dispute: do relational-attributes (المعنوية) also have a relation? The verifiers say no, and they give a logical argument against it. Understanding this definition and its rationale is essential for correctly applying the categories that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on definition and dispute
Focus on the sentences from 'وعرفوا التعلق' down to 'تصلح له'. Also read the earlier part where the author mentions the dispute between the verifiers and some mutakallimun.
The dispute is about which attributes have ta'alluq.
2
Identify the definition of ta'alluq
Find the sentence that literally defines ta'alluq. Write it down in Arabic and English. Notice the key phrase 'طلب الصفة أمراً زائداً على الذات'.
3
Understand the argument against both types having relation
The author gives a reductio ad absurdum: if both meaning-attributes and relational-attributes had relation, it would lead to two effective causes on one effect (e.g., in power and being powerful) and to 'attainment of the already attained' in knowledge and being knowing. Grasp why this is impossible.
This is a classic kalam argument against multiple independent causative factors.
4
Ask: why does this matter?
Reflect on why the scope of ta'alluq is so important. Without this restriction, the classification of relations would be incoherent, leading to theological absurdities.
This connects to the lesson's objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تعلقات الصفات تعلقات القدرة
٣٣ - فَقُدْرةٌ بِمُمْكِن تَعَلَّقَتْ بِلا تَنَاهِي مَا بِهِ تَعَلَّقَتْ
قوله : (فَقُدْرةٌ ... إلخ) أي : إذا أردت معرفة تعلقات الصفات، فأقول لك: (قدرة ... إلى آخره)، فالفاء فاء الفصيحة، ولما طوى ذيل مباحث الصفات، شرع في نشر ما لها من التعلقات .
والذي اعتمده المحققون أن التعلق للمعاني فقط، وقال بعض المتكلمين: للمعنوية، ولم يقل أحدٌ بأن التعلق للمعاني والمعنوية معاً، وإلا لزم اجتماع مؤثرين على أثر واحدٍ في القدرة والكون قادراً، والإرادة والكون مريداً، ولزم تحصيل الحاصل في العلم وكونه عالماً وهكذا الباقي، وعرفوا التعلق بأنه طلب الصفة أمراً زائداً على الذات تصلح له.
واعلم أن صفاتِ المعاني من حيث التعلق وعدمه، ومن حيث عموم التعلق للواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وخصوصه بالممكنات أو بالموجودات، أقسام أربعة : الأول : ما يتعلَّق بالممكنات ؛ وهو القدرة والإرادة ، لكن تعلُّق الأولى تعلُّق إيجاد وإعدام، وتعلُّق الثانية تعلُّق تخصيص.
والثاني: ما يتعلق بالواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وهو العلم والكلام، لكن تعلق الأولِ تعلق انكشاف، وتعلق الثاني تعلق دلالة.
والثالث : ما يتعلق بالموجودات، وهو السمع والبصر والإدراك، إن قيل به والرابع: ما لا يتعلق بشيء وهو الحياة، وقد ذكرها المصنف على هذا الترتيب كما ستراه، ومعرفة التعلقات غير واجبة على المكلَّف؛ لأنها من غوامض علم الكلام ، كما نقله الشيخ البَرَّاوي عن سيدي محمد الصغير، وذكره الشيخ الشنواني .
Explanation of the relations of attributes. The relations of power.
33 - A power relates to a possible, without limit to that which it relates.
His saying: (A power ... etc.) means: if you wish to know the relations of the attributes, I say to you: (power ... etc.), so the 'fa' is the 'fa' of eloquence. And when he folded the skirt of the discussions of attributes, he began to spread what pertains to them of relations.
And that upon which the verifiers have relied is that the relation is only for the meaning-attributes (المعاني), and some mutakallimun said: for the relational-attributes (المعنوية), and no one has said that the relation is for both the meaning-attributes and the relational-attributes together, because that would necessitate the conjunction of two effective causes on one effect in power and being powerful, and will and being willing, and would necessitate the attainment of the already attained in knowledge and being knowing, and likewise the rest. And they defined the relation as: a request by the attribute for an additional matter beyond the essence that it is suitable for.
And know that the attributes of meanings, in terms of relation and lack thereof, and in terms of the generality of relation to the necessary, the contingent, and the impossible, and its specificity to possibles or to existents, are four categories:
First: That which relates to possibles, and that is power and will, but the relation of the first is a relation of bringing into existence and annihilating, and the relation of the second is a relation of specification.
Second: That which relates to the necessary, the contingent, and the impossible, and that is knowledge and speech, but the relation of the first is a relation of disclosure, and the relation of the second is a relation of indication.
Third: That which relates to existents, and that is hearing, sight, and perception, if it is affirmed.
Fourth: That which does not relate to anything, and that is life. And the author has mentioned them in this order as you will see. And knowledge of the relations is not obligatory upon the legally responsible person, because they are among the subtleties of kalam, as narrated by al-Barrawi from Sayyidi Muhammad al-Saghir, and mentioned by al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'relation' (تعلق) of attributes and enumerates its types. It begins by introducing the section on relations of attributes, quoting the poem line about power relating to possibles. The commentary explains that the 'fa' is the 'fa' of eloquence, indicating that the author is now elaborating after previous discussion. Then the author states the scholarly consensus: relation applies only to the meaning-attributes (المعاني), i.e., the essential attributes like power, knowledge, will, etc., not to the relational attributes (المعنوية). He rejects the idea that both types have relation, as that would lead to multiple causative factors. Then he gives the definition of relation: it is a request by the attribute for an additional matter beyond the essence that it is suitable for. Finally, he classifies the four types of relation based on the objects of attributes. (1) Power and will relate to possibles, but power's relation is creative (إيجاد وإعدام) while will's is specification (تخصيص). (2) Knowledge and speech relate to the necessary, contingent, and impossible—knowledge discloses, speech indicates. (3) Hearing, sight, and perception (if affirmed) relate to existents. (4) Life has no relation at all. The author notes that knowing these relations is not obligatory, as it is a subtle matter of kalam.

Key Terms
التعلق
المعاني
المعنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that ta'alluq applies to both essential attributes (like power) and their derived properties (like being powerful).
Correction: The verifiers assert that ta'alluq is only for meaning-attributes; including relational-attributes would cause logical contradictions like having two effective causes for the same effect.

Checkpoint
According to the verifiers, which attributes have ta'alluq?
A) Only meaning-attributes (المعاني)
B) Only relational-attributes (المعنوية)
C) Both meaning-attributes and relational-attributes
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Ta'alluq is defined as the attribute's request for an extra matter beyond the essence, and it is only affirmed for meaning-attributes, not for relational-attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own attributes, do you notice that your power or knowledge often seeks something beyond yourself—a desire for more? How does this contrast with the self-sufficiency of Allah, whose attributes do not need an extra matter to be real but are purely relational? What does this teach you about your own dependency on creation?
?
The passage argues that if both meaning and relational attributes had relation, it would lead to impossibility. In your life, do you ever try to assign multiple ultimate causes to your spiritual states—attributing your faith both to your own effort and to divine grace as if they are independent? How does this lesson warn you against such dualism in tawheed?
?
Ta'alluq is defined as a 'request' by the attribute. Consider your own heart: what does it continually 'request' beyond your essence—status, comfort, validation? Are you willing to let those requests be shaped by the truth that only Allah is the object of all real relations? What would change in your daily actions if you truly believed that.

The Four Categories of Attribute Relations
Enumerates four categories of relations of meaning-attributes and notes their subtlety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four categories of relations of meaning-attributes and identify which attributes belong to each category.

Core Idea
Meaning-attributes relate to their objects in four distinct ways, from possibles to nothing at all.

Now that we know ta'alluq belongs only to meaning-attributes, the author classifies their relations based on the scope of their objects. Some attributes relate to possibles, others to all intelligible realities, others only to existents, and life remarkably has no relation at all. This classification deepens our understanding of how each divine attribute functions in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration of the four categories
Read the passage from 'واعلم أن صفاتِ المعاني...' to the end. Notice the author's careful wording: each category is defined by what the attribute relates to.
2
Identify the attributes in each category
For each category, list the attributes: first: power and will; second: knowledge and speech; third: hearing, sight, perception; fourth: life. Note the specific type of relation for each.
Power's relation is 'bringing into existence and annihilating'; will's is 'specification'.
3
Understand the objects of each category
First category relates to possibles (الممكنات); second relates to necessary, contingent, and impossible (الواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات); third to existents (الموجودات); fourth to nothing.
Knowledge's relation is 'disclosure' (انكشاف); speech's is 'indication' (دلالة).
4
Reflect on the non-obligatory note
The author concludes that knowing these relations is not obligatory for the legally responsible person because it is a subtlety of kalam. Ask yourself: why would the author include this disclaimer?
This highlights that such details are for advanced students, not general required belief.

?

How does this truth challenge your tendency to find your identity and worth in relationships, achievements, or what others think of you? What would it look like for you to root your sense of self entirely in God’s self-sufficient life?
?
Consider that God’s power relates only to possibles, not to impossibles. When you make duʿā’, do you sometimes ask for what is logically impossible (e.g., a contradiction), or do you trust God’s power within the realm of possibility? How can this understanding refine your dua and your reliance on God’s wisdom?

Power's Relation to Possibles: Eligibility vs Actual
Explains power's relation to possibles and introduces the eligibility/actual distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how divine power relates to all possibles, including those that will never occur, through the concept of eligibility relation.

Core Idea
Divine power relates to every possible, but to those that never occur, it relates by eligibility, not actuality.

This passage clarifies a nuance in the doctrine of divine power. While power extends to all possibles, how does it relate to things that Allah knows will never happen? The answer distinguishes between two types of relation: eligibility and actual. Understanding this preserves both divine power and foreknowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the source text and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms and the flow of the argument.
2
Understand the definition of 'possible'
The passage defines 'possible' as that whose existence or non-existence is not necessary in itself, even if it becomes necessary due to another. Grasp this before moving on.
This definition is crucial for the distinction that follows.
3
Identify the two types of relation
Find where the text introduces the distinction between 'talluq suluhi' (eligibility relation) and 'talluq tanjizi' (actual relation). Understand why the latter cannot apply to things that Allah knows will not occur.
The key phrase: 'تعلق صلوحي لا تنجيزي'.
4
See the reconciliation of two opinions
Notice how the author uses this distinction to reconcile the view that such things are within power and the view that they are not. The first opinion is correct if interpreted as eligibility.
This shows the practical theological importance of the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بِمُمْكِن تَعَلَّقَتْ الجار والمجرور متعلق بالفعل بعده، وإنما قدمه عليه لإفادة الحصر، فكأنه قال: لا تتعلق إلا بممكن؛ أي بكل ممكن، فالمراد العموم لأن النكرة في سياق الإثبات قد تعم، كما في قوله تعالى : عَلِمَتْ نَفْسٌ مَا أَحْضَرَتْ) التكوير : ١٤]؛ أي: كل نفس، فالقدرة متعلقة بجميع الممكنات؛ لأنه لو خرج ممكن عن تعلقها لزم منه العجز، وهو محال عليه تعالى.
في ذاته (1)
والمراد بالممكن : ما لا يجب وجوده ولا عدمه لذاته، ولو وجب وجوده أو عدمه لغيره، فالذي تعلَّق علمه تعالى بوجوده من الممكنات، فهو وإن كان ممكناً لكن وجب وجوده لغيره، كإيمانِ مَنْ علم الله إيمانه، والذي تعلق علمه تعالى بعدم وجوده، فهو وإن كان ممكناً في ذاته لكن وجب عدم وجوده لغيره، كإيمانِ مَنْ علم الله عدم إيمانه كأبي جهل، لكن تعلق القدرة بالذي تعلق علم الله بعدم وجوده.. تعلق صلوحي لا تنجيزي، وإلا لانقلب العلم جهلاً، وهو محال، وبذلك يجمع بين القولين، فالقول بأنه من متعلقاتِ القدرة محمول على أنه من متعلقاتها باعتبار التعلقِ
(1) في (ط): (علم).
His saying: (in a possible relates) — the preposition and its object are connected to the verb after it, and he advanced it over it to indicate restriction, as if he said: it does not relate except to a possible, i.e., to every possible. So the intended meaning is generality, because the indefinite noun in the context of affirmation may be general, as in His statement, exalted: 'Every soul knows what it has brought' (al-Takwir:14), i.e., every soul. So power is related to all possibles, because if a possible were outside its relation, impotence would follow, and that is impossible for Him, exalted.
In His essence (1)
And the meaning of 'possible' is: that whose existence and non-existence are not necessary in itself, even if its existence or non-existence becomes necessary due to another. So that whose existence His knowledge, exalted, has encompassed from among the possibles, even though it is possible, its existence becomes necessary due to another, like the faith of one whom Allah knows to have faith. And that whose non-existence His knowledge, exalted, has encompassed, even though it is possible in itself, its non-existence becomes necessary due to another, like the faith of one whom Allah knows will not have faith, like Abu Jahl. But the relation of power to that whose non-existence Allah has encompassed is a relation of eligibility (صلاحي) not actual (تنجيزي), otherwise knowledge would turn into ignorance, and that is impossible. And by that, reconciliation is made between the two sayings. So the saying that it is among the relations of power is interpreted as being among its relations in terms of the relation (of eligibility).
(1) In (T): (علم).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed analysis of how power (قدرة) relates to possibles, addressing a potential objection. The line under comment is 'قدرة بممكن تعلقت' meaning 'power relates to a possible.' The author emphasizes that the preposition and its object are advanced to indicate restriction: power relates only to possibles, and to every possible. The indefinite 'بممكن' is interpreted as general because it is in an affirmative context. He then clarifies what 'possible' means: something whose existence and non-existence are not necessary in themselves, even if they become necessary due to an external factor. For example, the faith of someone whom Allah knows will believe is possible in itself but becomes necessary due to Allah's knowledge. Similarly, the unbelief of someone like Abu Jahl is possible in itself but becomes necessary due to Allah's knowledge of its non-occurrence. However, power's relation to that which Allah knows will not occur is a relation of eligibility (تعلق صلاحي) not actual (تنجيزي). If power were related actually, it would imply that Allah's knowledge changes, which is impossible. This reconciles two opinions: one holding that such things are within power, the other that they are not. The first opinion is correct if interpreted as a relation of eligibility.

Key Terms
ممكن
تعلق صلاحي
تعلق تنجيزي
العجز
انقلاب العلم جهلاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that divine power cannot relate to things that will never happen, because they are impossible.
Correction: They are not impossible; they are possible in themselves. Power relates to them by eligibility, preserving divine foreknowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does power relate to that which Allah knows will not exist?
A) With an actual relation (تنجيزي)
B) With a relation of eligibility (صلاحي)
C) It does not relate at all
D) With a relation of necessity

Key Takeaway
Divine power relates to all possibles, but to those that will never occur, it is a relation of eligibility, not actuality, preserving divine foreknowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage explains that for those whose non-existence is known by God, His power relates to them only by eligibility, not actuality. This means that although something is possible in itself, it will never happen because God knows it won't. Consider your own faith: do you truly believe that your faith is a gift from God, and that He knows whether you will remain faithful until death? How does the reality that your entire spiritual journey is encompassed by divine knowledge change how you approach your daily acts of worship? Are you actively choosing to turn your potential faith into actual faith, or are you complacent? Urgently ask yourself: What concrete step will you take today to ensure that the possibility of your faith becomes an actuality?
?
The author uses the example of Abu Jahl to illustrate that even his unbelief, though possible in itself, was necessary due to God's knowledge. This teaches us that God's power and knowledge are perfectly consistent. Think about a time you doubted God's wisdom because something bad happened to you. Can you now see that even that event was within the realm of God's power, but He chose not to bring about a different outcome for a reason you may not understand? How can this lesson fortify your trust in God when you face trials? Commit to recite the lesson's principle whenever you feel doubt: 'His power relates to all possibles, but to those that never occur, it is a relation of eligibility, not actuality, preserving His knowledge.'
?
The distinction between eligibility and actuality is not just philosophical; it has a practical impact on how we understand our own intentions. You may intend to do good deeds, but only those that Allah knows will happen become actual. Does this realization humble you? Does it make you turn to Allah more often, asking Him to grant you success in acting upon your good intentions? Write down one intention you have had for a long time but never acted upon. Today, decide to turn that eligibility into actuality, relying on Allah's power.

8 min
Four Types of Divine Attributes by Attachment
The author classifies four types of divine attributes of meanings by attachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four categories of divine attributes of meanings based on what they attach to, and why knowing these details is not obligatory for every Muslim.

Core Idea
Divine attributes attach to different realities—some to possibles, some to all things, some to existents, and life to nothing.

The science of kalam carefully classifies divine attributes to avoid misunderstanding Allah's nature. This passage introduces a key classification: the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-maʿānī) are divided into four types depending on what they 'attach' to. Understanding this classification deepens theological precision, yet the author notes that such details are not required for every believer—they are part of the subtleties of kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a sense of the author's style and the flow of the classification. Then read the translation carefully.
Notice the definition of attachment at the beginning.
2
Identify the four divisions
List the four categories mentioned: those attaching to possible things, those attaching to necessary/possible/impossible, those attaching to existents, and that which attaches to nothing.
Each category includes specific attributes.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why this classification matters. It helps us understand how divine attributes relate to creation and to Allah's essence.
The note about non-obligatory knowledge shows the depth of kalam.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you can recall which attribute attaches to nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإلهيات الحاصل في العلم وكونه عالماً وهكذا الباقي، وعرفوا التعلق بأنه طلب الصفة أمراً زائداً على الذات تصلح له. واعلم أن صفاتِ المعاني من حيث التعلق وعدمه، ومن حيث عموم التعلق للواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وخصوصه بالممكنات أو بالموجودات، أقسام أربعة : الأول : ما يتعلَّق بالممكنات ؛ وهو القدرة والإرادة ، لكن تعلُّق الأولى تعلُّق إيجاد وإعدام، وتعلُّق الثانية تعلُّق تخصيص. والثاني: ما يتعلق بالواجبات والجائزات والمستحيلات، وهو العلم والكلام، لكن تعلق الأولِ تعلق انكشاف، وتعلق الثاني تعلق دلالة. والثالث : ما يتعلق بالموجودات، وهو السمع والبصر والإدراك، إن قيل به والرابع: ما لا يتعلق بشيء وهو الحياة، وقد ذكرها المصنف على هذا الترتيب كما ستراه، ومعرفة التعلقات غير واجبة على المكلَّف؛ لأنها من غوامض علم الكلام، كما نقله الشيخ البراوي عن سيدي محمد الصغير، وذكره الشيخ الشنواني.
The divine matters: what is obtained in knowledge and His being knowing, and likewise the rest. And they defined attachment (al-ta'alluq) as the attribute's seeking something additional to the essence that is suitable for it. And know that the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-maʿānī) from the perspective of attachment and non-attachment, and from the perspective of generality of attachment to necessary, possible, and impossible things, and its specificity to possible things or to existents, are four divisions: The first: what attaches to possible things – and it is power and will, but the attachment of the first is attachment of bringing into existence and annihilating, and the attachment of the second is attachment of specification. The second: what attaches to necessary, possible, and impossible things – and it is knowledge and speech, but the attachment of the first is attachment of disclosure, and the attachment of the second is attachment of indication. The third: what attaches to existents – and it is hearing, sight, and perception, if it be said. And the fourth: what does not attach to anything – and it is life. And the author (al-muṣannif) mentioned them in this order as you will see. And knowledge of the attachments is not obligatory upon the legally responsible person (al-mukallaf), because it is among the subtleties of the science of kalam, as transmitted by al-Shaykh al-Barrawi from Sayyidī Muḥammad al-Ṣaghīr, and mentioned by al-Shaykh al-Shanwānī.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a classification of divine attributes. It begins by defining attachment (ta'alluq) as the attribute's seeking something additional to the essence that is suitable for it. Then it states that the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-maʿānī) are divided into four types based on what they attach to: (1) those attaching to possible things (power and will) – power's attachment is bringing into existence and annihilating, will's attachment is specification; (2) those attaching to necessary, possible, and impossible things (knowledge and speech) – knowledge's attachment is disclosure, speech's attachment is indication; (3) those attaching to existents (hearing, sight, and perception, if accepted); (4) that which does not attach to anything (life). The author notes that the author of the matn (Jawharat al-Tawhid) mentioned them in this order. Finally, it clarifies that knowledge of these attachments is not obligatory for the mukallaf because they are among the subtleties of kalam, citing authorities.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All divine attributes attach to existent objects in the outside world.
Correction: Some attributes like knowledge attach to non-existent possibles and impossibles, and life attaches to nothing at all.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which attribute attaches to nothing?
A) Power
B) Knowledge
C) Life
D) Will

Key Takeaway
Divine attributes of meanings are of four types based on what they attach to: power and will to possibles, knowledge and speech to all three categories, hearing/sight/perception to existents, and life to nothing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage states that knowledge of these attachments is not obligatory because it is subtle. Are you content to leave some aspects of Allah's attributes as subtle and beyond your full comprehension, or do you feel a need to master every detail? What does that say about your heart's posture before Allah? Will you accept this limitation with humility, or does it unsettle you?
?
The attribute of life attaches to nothing. How does this affect your understanding of Allah's self-sufficiency? Do you truly believe that Allah's life is not dependent on anything, or do you still subconsciously think of His life in terms of your own? When you say 'al-Hayy' in your du'ā, do you reflect that He is alive without deriving life from anything?
?
Power attaches to both bringing into existence and annihilating. Have you ever truly realized that the same attribute that created you could annihilate you at any moment? Does this make you turn to Him in constant humility and fear, or do you live as if your existence is secure? What change will you make today because of this truth?
